# Thread: Guess I'm in
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/>
**Subforum:** My Optimal Journal
**Posts:** 329
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Peertje80 — 2015-04-25T18:15:34+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162406>

I was waiting for the rains to clear and the wind to pick up, so I could get some kite surfing done. I think it's going to take forever before it will. Rather slow moving depression over head. Might as well start my journal now.

My goal is to improve skin and eyes. Though doubts are still present in me, because I've been told this is as good as gets for a long time.

Anyway I always had skin issues. Rashes, heat rashes with blisters, contact allergy, latex allergy... kinda everything allergy, strange reactions that resulted in big patches of hard skin itching like hell, dry skin, acne, hand eczema, HS. It really is no telling what will come up next. I learned soon dermatologists are quacks.

I was born with strabismus of the left eye. This was corrected surgically at the age of 3. However later in childhood I developed isotropy of the right eye with a double picture. So another surgery was required to fix this at the age of 9. Till today I still have a very poor peripheral sight on the right, a hidden squint, shitty depth perception, sometimes blurred sight with black spots in vision, light sensitive (bright light hurt my eyes) and very tired eyes.

I all ready made some progress:

-   Quite smoking
-   Bought house with garden not far from the sea
-   Vetoed TV from bedroom
-   Went gluten and starch free
-   Be outside more (learned kite surfing)
-   Walk bare feet when ever possible
-   Quite BCP

So overall I think I'm pretty healthy and happy. But I worry about my persisting skin problems because nobody seems to know what causes it. And that just doesn't sit right by me. At the moment I weigh in at 196lbs standing 6 ft tall like a real Dutch giant. Gained massive amount of weight this winter, because my structured and regular life was interrupted with... well with some people not living any more actually. So if I would loose some weight along the way that wouldn't be too bad either.

So far not such a good start today:
I woke up at 7:00 AM, walked outside bare feet in my pyjama in the pouring rain to stare at the sky. My neighbour came outside to check on me, concerned something was wrong haha. Village life. I noticed the sky is exceptionally bright, even with the clouds and rain. Then break fast. Usually I have a large appetite, but today I just couldn't eat that much, small can of salmon topping it of with 2 spoons full fat Greek yoghurt. Went to market at 10:00 AM bought some things in the vitamin corner, some nuts to crack and checked in at the DHA counter. Did some house work and some study for exams on the 4th. Totally crashing at 15:30 PM. Forgot to have lunch. Plus we went out to eat yesterday. I accidentally ate some egg noodles. I thought they were rice noodles. I never eat noodles. Why did I do that? Now sun is shining and wind is blowing but no energy left for kite surfing. Maybe after diner.

### Peertje80 — 2015-04-26T11:14:57+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162449>

Yesterday evening after sun down, we made an assessment of our bedroom. After moving we still haven't found time and inspiration to buy curtains. The newspaper we stuck to the windows gave us some privacy but wasn't really blocking out the street lights. So we taped some black garbage bags to the windows to block as much light as possible. With the door closed, it was pretty dark. But we have to buy curtains, there is a lot of light from neighbouring houses, street lights and... lights from the greenhouses about a mile away.

Went to bed at 23:30 and woke up in a panic at 8:30. What time is it? I didn't hear the alarm (well it is Sunday, but I forgot no alarm today). Usually I wake up sometimes during the night to check time. But now I hadn't the slightest idea what time it was with the room being totally dark. Woke up with lots of energy, though with stiff lower back. Guess I'm not used to lay down for 9 hours straight. Wow 9 hours of straight sleep omg.

Walked outside barefeet to stare at the sky. No sun, misty and rainy yet again. Nice intense white sky though. Then break fast: 5 egg nori omelet with mushrooms, parsley, some fresh mackerel and some full fat Greek yoghurt with some nuts with BP coffee.
Now I have to do some study and wait till southern warm stream will turn north to bring in cold polar air and some decent wind to kite later this day. Some sun would be nice too, but I guess that is too much to ask for.

So I found a new goal: buy curtains stat.

### Linz — 2015-04-26T11:18:48+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162451>

Welcome Peertje,

To help your skin you need lots of DHA, good water and foods with sulphur (pork/bacon/onions). Balance your vitamin D and A cycles with very careful attention to natural light and seasonal food as well as gluten-free. do have a look at the blogs on sulphated cholesterol and vitamin D if you haven't already read them.

Crossed your post this morning. You seem to have a great grasp of this already!

Thank you Linz. I will take a look at sulphated cholesterol stuff. But I have to contain myself and study first for my exams and not spend all my time reading other stuff .

I think I got the DHA down since a week or 2. Found out I can buy fresh fish just around the corner of my work place. So I'm not taking any lunch to work but buy there. Herring, mackerel, shrimp, salmon, you can get a good meal there for under 5 euros.
I already eat a fair amount of pork, bacon and unions. Salted herring with raw unions and pickles is how we eat our fish here. I will post a picture some day.

The good water thing still is a bit fuzzy for me. Our tap water is pretty clean. Well at least they don't add fluoride or chloride to the water. I have to investigate some more to decide if tap water is a no-go. But to be safe I now take 1 litre of mineral water to work everyday. It has a double function, because so much water equals lot of walking to restroom for me. I'm not used to drinking this much. In the morning I drink some cups of coffee and after noon some tea, tap water with meals. But that was it actually. Never really been in to soda's or juices.

Yes I have to be strict about gluten. Friday nights slippery noodles cost me dearly. It gave me some itchy small blisters on my left foot and intestinal discomfort.

what is your nnEMF at work? at home?

### Peertje80 — 2015-04-26T14:22:43+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162459>

> [caroline said:](/goto/post?id=162456)
>
> what is your nnEMF at work? at home?

Thank you caroline.

At work? I don't want to talk about it really. When I started in my current position, my work place was located in an old building in the woods not far from the sea. I worked at ground level with view on the trees. I could even open a window. It was really nice.

However the building didn't meet regulation criteria (go figure), so we had to move. They build a complete new building in the city centre, right next to... a rail road station. Great, right? I now work at the 6th floor, behind a window with no sun screen option. The artificial light above my head is a real pain. Because of my eye problems I see the light vibrate all the time. My complaint about the lighting... well the answer was it meet regulations. And nobody else seem to have any problems with it.

The walls and ceilings are bright white. Even the floors used to be white carpet. I just wanna die within 5 minutes after entering the building, there is so much light. We don't have offices any more but office gardens (as it's dubbed) So I'm in room with more than 60 pc's, twice as much screens and desk phones, cell phones and far tooo many people for my liking. And also as of late, we have company wi-fi across the building. And of course climate control. So were to begin here? Management is scratching their head why sick leave has sky-rocketed since we moved. My hand eczema started just a few weeks after the move. I never really considered it to be the cause till recently. But when I think of it, it was a quite noticeable event. Though I have many skin issues, I never had eczema.

We once had a power failure in the building. Everything was turned off. Such a quiet and peaceful experience \*sigh\*. I was amazed how much of difference it made to the senses.

But it is not all bad. I'm a 'child' from a newer generations. My application to work from my own home has been granted some months ago. So I can now work at home 2 days a week and I only have to visit the hell hole 3 days a week.

At home all pc's and gadgets are located in one room with cabled internet. We have wi-fi but I can (and do) turn it of easy. Dutch building law requires all houses have grounded electrical systems. So I think I'm save, but don't really know. I read about the smart meter thing, but I don't think it is an issue here (yet). We have an old fashion meter with the turning discs system (I don't know its technical name). I can disconnect every room separately from the net. I live on the edge of a village. I know of one small cell tower about a kilometre away. So at home, relatively ok, I think.

### Peertje80 — 2015-04-27T23:18:58+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162578>

So today was Kingsday. The 1 day in the year everybody in the Netherlands goes totally bananas dressed in orange. And it is a day off from work. Yeah!

I set alarm at 7:00 AM. Run down the other room to check wind status on my phone. Nothing... again. So went back to bed, but I was wide a wake. No use to stay in bed.
Put chair in outer corner of the garden, ate break fast and sipped coffee in the sun. Yes the sun was shining! After 30 minutes I went inside. The wind picked up so it started to get chilly.

At 10:30 AM at the beach. Setting up gear, ready to fly. Spoke with a young bald male. He was a beginner and it was his first session for this year. I asked where his cap, shoes, gloves and earplugs were. I got a blank face reply. He didn't need it because he doesn't kite surf in winter. At this point I wanted to slap him in the face. Spring hasn't started yet at sea. Northern polar wind, 48 degrees air temperature with a water temperature to match and a wind chill of 39. Not really Brazilian summer time circumstances. He was gonna give it try anyway.

Drank 1/2 litre of cold water and went in with summer suit, no cap, no gloves, no shoes. Had husband keep an eye out. Set my timer at 30 minutes. Practised some back rolls which I landed face down flat in the water. I couldn't finish the 30 minutes kiting. The cold wasn't too bad. I actually had pretty warm feet, but my right hand went numb from wind chill. So I stopped.

When I was warming up I saw the bald beginner returning to the kite landing zone. He walked like he was totally drunk. I went downstairs to go check on him, but he already passed out. He had kiters brain freeze. He was longer in the water then me. Because he is a beginner, he was in the rip tide washer the whole time. Going under water more then staying above. After a few seconds he woke up. He was nauseous and had wobbly legs. We put a cap on him and an emergency blanket. Warmed him up with tea. He was just fine, but hopefully learned his lesson not to mess about in this cold untrained and unprepared. Though it looks like summer, it is not.

### Peertje80 — 2015-04-28T23:25:24+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-162694>

So today no sun gazing. It was pouring down with hail and 34 degrees out side . I thought it was spring...

Went for BP and heart rate check up to my MP today. Last year I had a kiting accident. Went to see MP, ended up being rushed to hospital by ambulance because of suspicion of internal bleeding. I felt fine, just had a terrible pain on the right side. Well apparently I had a very slow heart rate, like 45 beats a minute and an immensely high blood pressure. Today my resting heart rate was still not so good with only 49 beats. BP was right on the mark 120/80. MP is pushing to direct to cardiologist to find cause since I'm not a professional endurance athlete and blood work didn't show anything. But I'm not feeling any negative effects, not dizzy or anything. Maybe I should decaffeinate first before going all medical? I drink quiet all lot of coffee. Should I even worry. I mean do I belong to the group "could drop dead suddenly"? Can you get slow heart rate from meditating? I don't know. Maybe sleep on it for a while first.

However I'm really light skinned. When I was in Japan they called me kinpatsu no kami. Golden hairs . Referring to the first red headed and sickly pale looking Dutch arriving after many months at sea some 400 years ago.

My mother picked my first name, which means " the pale one", with accurate pre-vision. She taught me to stay in the shades, use thick layers of sun screen and wear hats and long t-shirts during swimming. As a kid I got sun burned all the time. I was even hospitalized once for second degree burns from the sun exposure. Sometime I wonder if I was uncoupled since birth. Or maybe my mother was uncoupled and thus was I. Is that even possible? So it is really scary for me to expose parts that haven't been exposed in over ... well 25 years. So I feel I have to take baby steps first. BUt of course you're absolutely right

### Peertje80 — 2015-05-07T23:32:11+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-163549>

So small recap:

-   4 weeks in to leptin reset
-   increased seafood to minimal once a day sometimes twice a day (herring, mackerel, salmon, sardines, shrimps, mussels)
-   Using gunner glasses when working and during screen time in evening
-   After sunset minimal light lit in house (still have to buy curtains though)
-   No sunglasses while commuting to work early morning
-   Sungazing with breathing exercise after waking up (works better now for me now that the sun is also up early)
-   Use smokers break to get 5 minutes of rays at 9AM when working at the office
-   Use coffee break when working at home to get 15 minutes outside at 10AM minimally dressed (lucky it is getting warmer now)
-   Cut coffee from 10> cups to 3 or 4 cups (just can't do less yet)
-   Increased water intake from 500 ml to 1500 ml (lot of movement going back and forth to toilet. So increased exercise too)
-   try to do some yard work after work around 16:30 to get more sun light.
-   No TV
-   Sealed bedroom from light
-   CT is less now sea is warming up, switched to morning showers and evening face ct. (But should I stop that now I can use light again?)

Results so far are strange:

-   I suffered a injury on my foot. Quite a big wound actually. But it is healing like crazy fast. I hardly believe it myself but you can almost see it healing while looking at it(?)
-   Shedding skin on my face, hands and feet
-   My energy crashes sometimes really big (instead of up and down) and I have to take a nap. So I do. There after I feel better.
-   Since 2 days I can skip lunch without effort. Just a bit hungry around 16:30 (dinners has to wait till 18:00 for social reasons). When drinking big glass of water it disappears. This seemed impossible 4 weeks ago. I felt I was in a constant state of ravenousness after mourning and stress full period during winter.
-   Sleep is better but still not very consistent. But at least I do have some nights of uninterrupted sleep now. Which is so... precious.
-   My nails are getting super tough and are growing faster then usual.
-   My eyes feel much more relaxed at work. No more pinching against the light. It improves my mood at work considerable. Down side of this seems to be I squint a whole lot more. My right eye seems to be all over the place. I hope it is transitional.
-   I'm getting a nice tan first time ever.
-   Some acne on my back which I do not have normally.
-   My HS... I don't know. Don't wanna jump the gun, but it seems to be in remission for about 1 week now. The active infections are disappearing, no hard lumps under skin to be found. Just had 1 tiny fistula come up, break and disappear in light speed fashion. I have to wait a full cycle to believe it I think.
-   Bouncing back from stopping with BCP unexpectedly well. Especially mood wise.
-   My thinking is changing (can this happen even). Instead of "picture thinking" I now use stories to think more. This is a really nice perk for my work. Words come easier that way.
-   My resting heart rate is now 58 bpm. Which is not great still, but at least better then being under 50. I think I would be please with 60> And I hope it makes me feel less like torturous while exercising.
-   Weight loss is minimal 1 kilo so far (I cheated and drank some glasses of alcohol during festivities. Had some potatoes too). But I need to buy new wetsuit because it's not tight around my legs any more. And it was and should be! I noticed the same for my jeans, so legs seem to be shrinking somehow.

Thing to do:

-   Read Ubi 12
-   Find out about tapwater
-   Continue reset for few more weeks I guess.
-   Now go to bed.....

### Peertje80 — 2015-05-10T01:48:06+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-163748>

Today I had to look up something in my diary from a while back. I came across a passage were I described what happens when I got an itch attack on my hands at night (this remained even after the hand eczema was long gone).

How wonderful is the human mind for forgetting all this torture?

I know pain, but itch... It drove me crazy even to the point of self mutilation. A common attack would start early in the evening. My hands would feel warm, veins popping up, red skin. I would get a small itch and scratch it a bit. With in minutes small vesicula would appear. I scratch some more. With focus, breathing and sometimes meditation I could manage to stop scratching.

However after I went to sleep the itch would wake me up. I felt stress hormones pumping through my body like it was pouring out of my ears, feeling all hot and agitated. And the itch... unbearable. I would scratch my skin until it bled and then... some more. This wasn't enough to stop the itching. I would bang my head against the wall out of fear and frustration. One night I even took a small potato knife and scratch away layers of dry and mutilated skin. Or put my hands in almost too hot water.

When I got to the doctors office the day after he would give me some creams with steroids for the billionth time. Not working, it did absolutely nothing for me. And this was my fault they said. I wasn't applying enough or some other excuse why this wouldn't work. I applied a crap pile of this stuff without any effect. Nothing really helped. Till someone mentioned cold water worked for him. But not just cold water... no really really really cold water. So I tried and it worked. I put my hands on ice if they get itchy. After moving into my new house the night time itch disappeared all together. That really puts environment in perspective for me for the second time in my live.

So CT really took my interest and this is how I ended up on Dr Jacks website eventually. Though with my interest for paleo I visited before, but it was too difficult for me to make sense of any of the content back then. With all the strange changes in my body right now (seems like puberty all over again in some funky way) I'm even more determined. I knew I wasn't crazy... something outside of me caused this torture. So glad to have found this explained why (and hoping to understand it completely one day). I aiming at complete remission of HS and my tortured and broken skin. I really feel it is in my grasp now!

Way too long story again, sorry

This was 1 year ago. I still have dry skin on my hands but way better than in this picture.
[](https://forum.jackkruse.com/attachments/last-june-jpg.1846/)

### Lahelada — 2015-05-25T18:37:06+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-165304>

Lol,sorry I confused you there . BPC = Bulletproof coffee, depreciating remark about myself that the caffeine had not reached the parts other drinks cannot reach and that my focus was off .
Organisational Structural Failure 1 is a blog of the doc's . I will find you the url in a minute.
I commented on stress as you see your karate exercise as a physical muscle stress so you think glucosamine. The story usually starts long before then as you just pointed out when you remembered the unexplained shoulder pain. I started my diary notbeing able to carry heavy sling over the shoulder shopping bags . I thought age, wear and tear and here I was told cortisol. I did not get the light water EMF then but just now when ou asked about glucosamine I was thinking maybe I could save you some "learning miles" A direct symptom reliever is almost always a "have a hammer will fix things with a nail approach" When you stand back you see that it is the whole house that needs rebuilding. You are doing a lot already ,kudos but as we are now wont to do and have been trained it would be treating a ymptom rather than the problem .
My shoulder pain started on the right side, following the pain in the right ankle . I am right handed. Look at the psychological stress but also the environment stress you are under. Quite often the psychological stress " the arguing as to why the neighbour who parks outside your house does not colourcoordinate his car with your garden fence" syndrome for example  a lot of middle aged people are given to ,is actually a product of environment stress.
I hope that makes more sense .

@[Cpt.Tired](https://forum.jackkruse.com/members/12957/) :

Blue blockers and dimming lights make a big difference for me now. I used to be plugged in 12 hours a day (2 pc screens or/and tv or/and phone/ipad), sometimes more. Also I spend a lot of evenings in fluorescent light. If I don't wear blue blockers at night and bright light is on, my sleep is screwed and usually the day after I'm ravenous for carbs. I thought this cannot have such a instant effect for me, but I tried is several times now and the effect is (like) clock work. For me: Bright light at night=screwed sleep=need carbs/ more meals to sustain me through the day.

Boredom and coffee. Interesting concept. Back in the day (lol) when I used to smoke, I had the same thing when bored. Nothing to occupy your mind? Waiting for something or someone? Let's have cig. Or 2,3, 4...

### Peertje80 — 2015-06-20T14:59:22+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-169037>

I totally appreciate the fact of my car breaking down just when I was about to turn on to the highway. This is the nature of being. Things are until they break down, fall apart and disintegrate in to something else and so cease to exist as they were. I have a deep respect and admiration of the nature of things. But of course it is very coincidental it happened just at the moment I really needed my car. It couldn't have happened last week or the week before. No, it had to happen right now at the most inconvenienced time ever.

I could go full rpm with hardly any capacity from the engine(this sounds familiar somehow). I went straight to the dealer for repairs. Well actually it was more like a crawling pace of 30 km/h. The dealers is located quite some miles from my house, so I had to take the bus back home. I pulled out my smartphone and enabled 3g (I've not advanced to 4g). Trying to find the bus schedule and which transits I should take. No signal. The one time that I need to use my smartphone I have no signal what so ever. No wifi either. I'm in the middle of f\*\*\* nowhere. The irony of this made me laugh out loud. This made the people at the bus stop look very uncomfortable...

I needed to buy a bus ticket which is nowaday easier said then done. Because we have the transit chip card you have to slide over a reader at the door. I made some small talk with the very friendly bus driver lady and turned to take a seat in the bus... Fear struck my heart. OMG nobody warned me the zombie apocalypse is here! A bus full of people and not a sound. Heads all facing down, staring at their phone or tablet. If I would have walked in naked nobody would have noticed. It made the hairs on my arms and neck stand up. This was no good place to be.

When I got home my energy was totally drained from this strange adventure. I took a 20 minute nap to recuperate. And now I'm trying to make peace with the fact I can't execute the things I had to do.

### Lahelada — 2015-07-17T04:23:50+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-172159>

Hiya Peertje, mind occupied with sad things made me think of this . It is from Jack's facebook. I hope it is somehow applicable to your ruminating sad thoughts . Sending this on a hunch
"
****[Dr. Jack Kruse](https://m.facebook.com/drjackkruse?__tn__=C)****
[June 30, 2013 at 6:08am](https://m.facebook.com/story.php?story_fbid=545121775552181&id=239883926075969) ·

I don't dwell on anything from the past because the past is moment already gone. I only focus on the present moment because it is the only moment that I can have an effect on by what I choose to do. At any given moment in our lives, there are certain things that could have happened but didn't or won't. The real magic moments often go unrecognized in the present, and then suddenly later it dawns on you that the hand of destiny changes everything in the path you are on. The past can never do that to us unless we allow it too. If you allow the past to "flavor" your current thoughts, the past becomes a drag on your future destiny. Past thoughts are just old gambles or risks in the "game of life". Past performance has no bearing on future gains in anything in life, contrary to what believe about the past. The past best serves us for learning about errors we made in judgment about events already unfolded. This lesson can be reapplied in the new reality, called our future, if we decide to use the lesson learned in the present as reality unfolds. If you are not willing to risk the 'usual' in the present, you will have to settle for the ordinary in your future. It is time to cut the rope on the past and focus on what you can control..........the now.

### Peertje80 — 2015-07-19T01:17:44+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-172316>

Today I choose it to be a good day

Well I think I had a summer cold anyway. Yesterday I felt shortness of breath. Duck diving during surfing was a bitch, but with spring tide it was necessary to survive rip tide. Even before my face hit the water I felt suffocated. While I usually stay under for 2 minutes easy (even when I was a hard core smoker). Anyway today my voice has returned to normal and I'm breathing just fine.

However something good is going on. I broke my kitesurfing jump height record... well broke it? I just F\*^^% smashed it. From 4,5 meters, I'm now at 9,8 meters. You know how high that is? That is a 3 story building  I was scared like hell though and immediately stopped surfing after that jump. Kinda of risky to crash from that height

Today I had to deal with my own stupidity. Went to pick up some stuff at a friends house. Normally it is not even a 1 hours drive, but today was a good day to do some road maintenance and close all tunnels in the direction I was heading. Leaving me in the car for 3 hours pulling up, breaking and standing still in the middle of the day in the blistering sun. Sure this is doable, maybe I would just suffer a mild case of road rage. But I came totally unprepared... I didn't bring any water  Shrivelled and over heated I returned home from my mission.

I drank some warm water, because I can't stand ice cold water when I haven't had a drink in a while. Then some food. My stomach made little sounds of joy when I broke my 12 hour fast. LOL some months ago my stomach was always loud and nagging, I now was surprised by the noise. I forgot it could make such incredible sounds.

Pssst did I tell you I have no active HS inflammation today?

### Peertje80 — 2015-07-20T23:44:35+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-172453>

Thanks caroline and b612

Yesterday I ate a Snickers for diner  ... this was the most """optimal""" choice available at the club I surf at. Which is absolutely ridiculous for a sports club of course.

I had BAB around 8AM and no lunch, because I don't need lunch any more. The entire morning it had been pouring cats and dogs, so I was getting ready to spend a lazy Sunday afternoon. At 1PM the sun came out. Sudden sun after a rainy morning... yes that means wind... lots of it. So we went to the beach to enjoy some kite surfing quality time. However the wind refused to die, it kept blowing. It was an insanely good session.

I had a lot of energy to spare and just had 2 water breaks. After 5 hours or so I had to quit because of the rolling thunder coming in. It was 8:30PM. I didn't have anything to eat for quite sometime and now I was in doubt what to do. I felt empty, not really hungry, but vaguely empty. I thought I needed to eat (or else what?). So I took something with carbs and without gluten (I think). The other options were carbs with gluten and some more carbs with sugar and gluten. I stuffed my face with the Snicker feeling like I committed a sin against my body. Letting it work so hard and feeding it such poor fuel. Well... it didn't do anything for me... I realized I could have done without it.

So I really believed I had to do that, but the truth was shockingly different. I could have managed without eating until BAB even with the amount energy spend kite surfing (which is said to be between 600 and 800 calories an hour depending on intensity). So I burned trough, let say 3000 calories of fuel on an empty stomach minus 1 Snickers. O yes and it didn't do shit for my weight, it was exactly the same as the morning before. Lesson learned.

Yesterday I had my first try at oysters. To great joy of my hubby who triumphantly filmed the whole process of hesitation to the actual downing of the poor creature.

This weekend will be all about resting. Bad weather this weekend. Today we have a big storm hitting us. Such storms in summer are called "canal rats", because they are pushed trough the canal between France and Britain. They are really quit dooms day like. Hitting our coast straight on with 50+ knots (bft 10 or more). Will be flying out of our panties. Time to hold on tight.

PS: I still have no active hidradenitis suppurativa. It has almost been a week Just have 1 small lump, which I aspect to go change in an active fistula. But maybe not, sometimes they just disappear on me.

### Peertje80 — 2015-07-28T23:19:22+0300

I can get my own if I want to, but doubt if they are any good because the grow in a drainage canal which is used to fluid excess water from the city sewage and polders when it is raining. Or else we would get wet feet sort to say.

After work today I was just sitting... you know contemplating world problems or to do laundry or not. Nobody home, lots and lots of rain.\*SIGH\* that rain is really a pain in the ^%$. It's been raining since Friday.

Then I noticed an enormous vein popping up in my left arm. That was never there before! I first panicked. Because this is what you do if your body is slowly morphing to optimal which is completely foreign to me. But then I thought this is actually pretty cool. I think this is a good thing right? I can get more out of sunlight? Or is it popping up because I take extraordinary measure to get more sunlight? Well if standing in the pouring rain at 6AM falls in to the category of "exposed to sunlight". Never mind, it is good morning CT for free.

### Peertje80 — 2015-08-13T22:51:41+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-174631>

So I had some deep shit to go through. This happens when in mourning... it has got too many stages. I have been there too many times already. And it is a place I will visit soon again. This is the human condition.
But for now that I have regained the faculty of my own mind... a realisation hit me hard. Like a smack in the face actually. I'm B.O.R.E.D. Big time.

After I had to make a career change from being a registered nurse, I just ended up somewhere career wise. And I made good money. I was comfortable. So it didn't bother me much. But now it does. I'm so totally f\*&%$ bored out of my mind I might as well be dead. Well not that I have a death wish. Au contraire. But I'm bored... very much so. 40 hours of boredom is just like prison. Or at least this is how I imagine prison to be.

I had to train someone on the job. I realized my job was too hard, he didn't understand. I tried to understand why he couldn't do it. I drew a blank. Then an other co-worker said: "You must have realized before that you are just a visitor here. We don't expect you to stick around very long. You did nursing school, went to university and a bunch of other stuff. Do you really feel passion for what you do now? For you this is just a way station. You are working way beneath your abilities. Why are you still here?" I know this was meant as a compliment somehow, but it really hurt. My job already kinda took leave from me at that moment.

Yes why am I still there? I'm really good at my job but... I have no passion for what I do. I have no motivation. I don't create anything and I don't make a difference. It has no meaning to me. There is no balance within like this (because my private life is awesome you know). So I though I can do pretty much anything else. I can do everything. I have to do something else. But it has to matter to me somehow...

This really feels like a step backward, but I know it will be a step forward. I have to quite my job. And I decided to make this a reality within a year. Because I now need an outlook on a change of career to make it through the day. Or is this just stuff that happens in my head when there is no surf? No this is real, it is time to bail. I'll figure it out.

Other wise: I'm doing fine. My HS is doormat for about a month now. No flare ups, no fistulas. It is almost insane. The skin on my hands is improving. I didn't shed skin in about 2 months. Slowly my skin is getting softer. Weight loss? Hmm not so much. I really like summer fruit a lot. But now days are getting shorter fast, I'm minding my carbs so to speak. I got this amazing tan from sitting naked in the sun whenever I can. I feel I will be a hundred years old someday.

### Cpt.Tired — 2015-08-14T00:25:53+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-174636>

I fully understand you about boredom at work. But with me it's a bit different. For me I'm not really good at what I do because my brain processing is slow. I know I have lots of potential because I'm well educated but fatigue, anxiety, cloudy thinking, low motivation and depression all come packaged together for me and makes me appear 'dumb'to my co-workers.
Everyone in my immediate area (3 people) seem to have issues with memory, logic and communication. I have the memory one and brain fatigue. They have far more energy mentally than me so they always 'win' in any debate.
But on a good day my performance rocks.
It has improved quite a bit lately I think because I started doing the 'Marty Hinz amino acid protocol'. L-Tyrosine with 5-HTP and L-Cysteine at pretty high doses spread throughout the day. It appears so far that all the above issues have become less now. I feel that my potential is slowly starting to emerge. I have a feeling that if I stick to this for a while I'll be able to get myself off of all medication
Dr Kruse talked about this protocol a bit in the webinar on the 'Epi-Paleo diet' (July 2012)
I started digging deeper into it. It's a fairly new mode of treatment that looks quite promising so, of course, a lot of the info is 'hidden'.

### Jack Kruse — 2015-08-15T15:56:50+0300

> [Peertje80 said:](/goto/post?id=174631)
>
> So I had some deep shit to go through. This happens when in mourning... it has got too many stages. I have been there too many times already. And it is a place I will visit soon again. This is the human condition.
> But for now that I have regained the faculty of my own mind... a realisation hit me hard. Like a smack in the face actually. I'm B.O.R.E.D. Big time.
>
> After I had to make a career change from being a registered nurse, I just ended up somewhere career wise. And I made good money. I was comfortable. So it didn't bother me much. But now it does. I'm so totally f\*&%$ bored out of my mind I might as well be dead. Well not that I have a death wish. Au contraire. But I'm bored... very much so. 40 hours of boredom is just like prison. Or at least this is how I imagine prison to be.
>
> I had to train someone on the job. I realized my job was too hard, he didn't understand. I tried to understand why he couldn't do it. I drew a blank. Then an other co-worker said: "You must have realized before that you are just a visitor here. We don't expect you to stick around very long. You did nursing school, went to university and a bunch of other stuff. Do you really feel passion for what you do now? For you this is just a way station. You are working way beneath your abilities. Why are you still here?" I know this was meant as a compliment somehow, but it really hurt. My job already kinda took leave from me at that moment.
>
> Yes why am I still there? I'm really good at my job but... I have no passion for what I do. I have no motivation. I don't create anything and I don't make a difference. It has no meaning to me. There is no balance within like this (because my private life is awesome you know). So I though I can do pretty much anything else. I can do everything. I have to do something else. But it has to matter to me somehow...
>
> This really feels like a step backward, but I know it will be a step forward. I have to quite my job. And I decided to make this a reality within a year. Because I now need an outlook on a change of career to make it through the day. Or is this just stuff that happens in my head when there is no surf? No this is real, it is time to bail. I'll figure it out.
>
> Other wise: I'm doing fine. My HS is doormat for about a month now. No flare ups, no fistulas. It is almost insane. The skin on my hands is improving. I didn't shed skin in about 2 months. Slowly my skin is getting softer. Weight loss? Hmm not so much. I really like summer fruit a lot. But now days are getting shorter fast, I'm minding my carbs so to speak. I got this amazing tan from sitting naked in the sun whenever I can. I feel I will be a hundred years old someday.

Saying you're bored’ tells me more about you and a lot less about your environment. It is an utterly useless thing to say out loud or to yourself. This attitude will always block you from optimal. You live in a great, big, vast world that you’ve seen and sampled like 0.000000000001 percent of it. Have you every thought of it this way? No. You are looking at your life with a negative lens and not a positive one.
Think of every single thing that happens in your life as an information upload to your mind. It is neither good or bad, just information. How your eyes and mind perceive it is how your mind will use it. When I read this and saw you were a nurse I know why you feel the way you do. I used to feel the same way until I realized the way I thought about things was my greatest deficit.
**_Success can manifest the moment you realize that no one is your enemy, except yourself._** You have always been the ingredient in the recipe of success. Only ignorant people walk away from inner greatness. Even the inside of your own mind is endless; it goes on forever, inwardly, do you understand just how much you're missing when say what you just said? The fact that you’re alive is amazing in and of itself, so you don’t get to say ‘I’m bored.” Change your ideas and your current life will also morph.

### Jack Kruse — 2015-08-15T16:04:01+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-174747>

The miracle of our brain's physiology isn’t that you can see the world as it is. It’s that you can see the world as it isn’t. Boredom occurs because you have not tapped the owner's manual in that brain. My job is to explain what you can't see but physics has observed to exist. Absence of evidence in a biology book is not absence of effect.
Raise your quality standards as high as you can live with, avoid wasting your time on routine problems and routine thinkers, and always try to work as closely as possible at the boundary of your abilities. Attack your comfort zone and disturb conformity with curiosity. Do this, because it is the only way of discovering how that boundary should be moved forward.
Mediocrity is boredom in disguise. It is not something to embrace, it is something to run away from.

**_Good is the enemy of great._** Good breeds boredom. Is detachment from the top the way to grow your ideas? This isn’t a question of right or wrong as much as it’s a question of good or great. Ponder that. Bad decisions made with good intentions, are still bad decisions. Never settle. Once you do you've lost. I see a lot of bad thinking in this thread right now and it is time to shake you out this. I want people seeing this thread to understand where boredom comes.........it comes from within and not outside.

To stay on the theme... I had a small reunion last night with some friends from college. It was great to see everybody again. And it surprised me to find out they struggle the same struggle. I understand now that standing still, no matter in what part of your life, means to perish somehow. Life is changing continuously. When you refuse to change (voluntary or involuntarily), you disconnect from life all together. So we not only need to stay connected to nature biologically or physically, but also mentally we need to connect to the very essence of nature.

### Peertje80 — 2015-08-25T00:29:42+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-175580>

We had a lot of rain last night. When I drove off on my bike the sun just came through. Chasing away the last clouds with its warmth. Illuminating the fields were I followed the meandering bike path to the city. The warm yellowish light reflected on a haze over the fields. Resulting in small but magical world around me. What better way to start a day? 30 minutes of magic and some relaxing exercise just before work. The shade of light reminded me that autumn is very near now. The news even reported a tornado today. But I guess the media should choose there words for such weather phenomena more wisely. It was a whirlwind at most. Big storms? Hmm okay we got our share. However when a tornado hits our side of the continent, the world must be really upside down I think.

### Peertje80 — 2015-08-25T23:08:13+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-175726>

I knew the question was coming. There was plenty of time to prepare and arrange my thoughts on the subject. This was the moment I was waiting for. My resistance against the ongoing violation of my biological being. After WIFI and double screens. This is the next thing: Bianca would you like to work longer hours in winter and take more leave during summer?

Well this question comes from the known fact our business is busiest in autumn/winter because of circumstance. The prospect of more time off during summer almost did me in. You see, I have more time for surfing then. Something that I really love to do. But however tempting, I said no.

Well actually I said: "Are you insane? Is this company on the outlook for a sharp increase in sick leave? Did we buy stock in health care? Are you out of it? Do you know what autumn and winter means in reality to a human being here on the north side of this rock called earth? Days are shorter. And you are thinking working longer is smart then. I will not see any day light what so ever. Are you trying to kill me. Is this is a serious question? Is it biological logical to work longer when days are shorter and people really want to hibernate. So you want to expose me to even more artificial light. Can I sue you when I get cancer from prolonged exposure to blue light and a lack of the natural one? Or maybe I should not, because by then I've cost you tons of money due to a lack of efficiency for years because my internal clocks don't run like they should and my sleep is whacked and I'm stressing out like a \*&^ and I'm pissing of customers with my never ending whining due to a DHA depleted brain." Or something in that direction.

Reply: "...eh"

Me: "Change the circumstances of our business. Make it busy during summer. Then we talk."

Reply: "Eh... so you want to work longer hours but only during summer?"

Me: "No I want to work less over all for the same pay to make my working schedule more suitable to circadian and seasonal cycles so I can be more efficient, more service orientated and make more money for you."

I know for sure they probably now think that I am the crazy one.

### Peertje80 — 2015-11-21T23:39:24+0200
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-182487>

It's been a while since my last post. Life has been crazy. Well lets say I've put things in motion. I was thumbing through my notes and I thought I might share some of my observations from the optimal health perspective from my vacation in Brazil. But first... after 6 months trying to live epi paleo... I was truck with surprise. So I'll share that first.

Since 2 months or so I was starting to get head aches. Also I felt I had to bend over backwards to get a good view on my computer screen. So went to see the optometrist. I'm officially not myopic any more. I'm only left with cylinders in my prescription and a slight plus +0,5 for the right eye. Also gained the ability to use my right eye. So I've some depth perception now, which is really weird for me. Since I never had the ability to see depth. This really great. I can go down the escalator without losing balance, poor a glass without looking at it from the side and other brilliant stuff like that.

So Brazil... For me the time difference with Brazil is 4 hours earlier. When I arrived (travelling west) at my destination I felt I had a very late party, but was pretty ok after a 24 hours journey. I was at 4 degrees south of the equator. Here are my observations:

-   Never ever forget to put something (like socks) on your feet while kiteboarding in extreme uv when you're from high up north. I burned my toes severely the first day. Second degree burn (you know with the blisters) on my right toes. It healed with stellar speed in 5 days.
-   In the 2 weeks I was there, I didn't get used to the time difference. Woke up at 4:45 AM local time everyday no matter how late I went to bed. 4:45 AM was pretty much sunrise too. Also every night I woke around 2:00 AM (normally I don't wake up during the night).
-   U can sleep butt naked without covers and survive ( well at least in 28 degrees Celsius).
-   I was bare feet 90% of the time. And was mostly outside. Only sleeping was done inside. With exception of the night I spend in the hammock (not recommended).
-   I used very little sun screen, surfing in long sleeved shirts and pants for sun protection, I only used some on my face if surfing between 11:00 and 14:00.
-   I let my skin get use to the sun gradually, exposing first couple of days only for 15 minutes. After that I could last longer and even started to get tanned. This surprised me, being a pale skinned red head.
-   I have to stay gluten free (that was my only dietary demand for this holiday), but this is really difficult in Brasil (at least in the setting I was in, hotels/pousada). I had to skip one day of kiting because of a gluten mistake. Totally drained my energy and had a nice time observing Brazilian toilet manner in a public restroom.
-   Other than that it was really nice to notice I remained a good bristol score through out my vacation. Though I had to fart all the time  (too much starchy carbs?)
-   I had a bad out break of acne on my back. I think it was the vegetable oils they use for cooking. It started after 3 days and it lasted till 3 days after my return home.
-   I had tons of energy. My kiteboarding sessions were one and half hour twice a day, for 12 days in row and 1 toilet break day some where in between. Never had muscle soreness nor cramps.
-   I did my first kite loop ever.
-   My diet was fruit.... fruit and some more fruit and eggs. Some (not so fatty) fish, some meats, rice, beans and potatoes. Acai and sometimes a coconut. Hardly any vegetables, some lettuce (I had to skip the bread, pancakes, cereals, cake, milk, cheese, ham, pasta's and processed meats).
-   When you eat rice, I notice your teeth get some sticky film on them. I really hate that feeling. Happens with potatoes too, but less.
-   After 10 days I got canker sores in my mouth. My thinking got sluggish and I was making really stupid motor skill mistakes while kite boarding. I think this was due to a lag of proper fats in my diet.
-   I injured myself on the 12th day because I wasn't able to asses risks so well. Made a huge mistake while landing my kite. I nearly lost my finger. A kite line ripped my skin of clean, left me with a flesh wound of 1,5 cm on my right index finger.
-   The wound on my index finger also healed insanely fast. After 2 days it was closed, and after 4 days you could hardly see it was ever there. That must have been the light and sea water, cause my diet was really poor.
-   In Brasil 30 degrees Celsius feels really not that hot compared to 30 degrees here up north.
-   I kicked my coffee habit in a wink. When I got back only 1 cup of coffee made me feel sick and I had to visit the toilet instantly.
-   My hormones were way off I think, my cycle was shortened by 6 days.
-   During my flight back I was in a new plane. It had touch screens in the chairs. I ask the flight attended how to turn it of, but it couldn't be turned off . So I stared at a blue lit screen for 7 hours straight during the night (euh).

-   Travelling back left me with a pretty little jet lag. My core temp dropped till 36 degrees for 2 consecutive mornings after my return. Which for me is really low. I was cold and sleepy for about 4 days. I was wide awake during my flight back (so didn't take melatonin). Also had to fast for 24 hours because all the food contain gluten and I had to toss my own food at customs. Drank lots of water though. Up on my return I started CT immediately.
-   The sun in Brazil really lifted my spirits. I returned to the worst autumn weather ever. The days after my return were rainy, clouded, cold, dark and depressing. But I feel really radiant somehow.
-   I really wanted to stay

So that's it.

> I'm really wondering what it was I experienced and if I should worry about it.

Peertje, that sounds a bit like an ocular migraine. I had two in one day years ago, and I ended up losing my vision both times, for about 20 minutes, though the process was painless. I saw a sparkling "C" shape in the center of my vision, as I got tunnel vision. I lost my vision in the morning, and again in the evening of the same day. Back then, I used magnesium to prevent recurrence of the migraines, to good effect.

>
> H, do you wear gloves? Have you ever taken your skin temperature after a cold session?
> Great sport/Hobby.

No never took my temp. And yes I wear neoprene gloves. Otherwise the wind will chill your fingers too much and then you cannot hold the bar any more. In this picture I wear a dry suit, so you stay relatively warm (and dry) in it. I chose the dry suit for safety because of sub zero wind chill. Above zero I choose a wetsuit. Which is a different story, because you get... well wet. Also there are other factors to consider. I had sessions that my skin was pink till purple from the cold and I was really shivering my ass off when it wasn't even that cold. It has to do with dew point to outside temp that will also determine if you get cold. It is different than just submerge in the water, because your expose to the wind too.

Only after sunbathing my back religiously the last 2 weeks (we were lucky, cold but sunny uv3 or 4), it is now finally subduing.

Concerning weight loss not much to report. I stay pretty consistent at 89. Which in itself is remarkable, because usually my weight is going up and down during cycle. Sometimes with a 2 kg difference. So maybe nothing happening is something happening.

I seem to get attached to white chocolate. Weird thing, cause I don't really like the taste of it. Vanilla and sweet taste.. eugh. But sometimes I just need to eat it, so I take a piece. Then I'm over it. I should not eat it. White chocolate is crap. But I can't help but wonder why I crave this from time to time, and just a small piece satisfies.

### Peertje80 — 2016-07-07T21:47:32+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-198027>

Omg did I just made a huge leap forward? How to explain this one. I never thought it would happen, but I experienced a 'normal' physical response to stress/danger. Because of complex ptsd in childhood, I was never really able to react to certain situations. I always get a freeze response or was dissociating instead of fight/flied. Which is quiet convenient in some settings. But actually not so healthy for your body because there is no release of energy. And as far as I understand in this case you really have fucked HPA axis. Well it gave me trouble anyway, difficult to fully relax and always bothered by problematic muscle tone.

I consulted a army psychiatrist last year to see if I could make some head way with this problem, because it seemed I always got stuck in my body somehow. I tried multiple things but I didn't seem to make progress. About 2 months ago however I made a terrible mistake while kitesurfing. After I crashed waaaaaaaaaaaaay too hard, I just laid there in the water waiting for the beep in my ears to die down. There was totally no physical response whatsoever. After some days I noticed I injured my neck pretty bad. So I ended up at the physical therapist... again. He proposed to try and see if we could prompt a stress response anyway (without using TRE I might add because I find it too overwhelming). So I committed to physically exhaust myself by running, biking and weight lifting a couple of days straight before our next session to lower my threshold of control. Then he just very softly massaged my neck, shoulders and back. Though it didn't feel soft to me. More like someone putting his hand in my body to rearrange everything. However, before I knew what hit me I was shaking like crazy, heart pounding in my throat, feelings of distress and fear just flowing by. I tried to fight it.... fear of the unknown, but my therapist told me calmly just to let it go. So I did. After 15 minutes or so the response slowly stopped. I was dead tired, not able to lift a limb, and slept after for 1,5 hours like a rock.

The days after that session were even more disturbing (well at first anyway). I would already start to shake and feel nauseous with something benign like a phone ringing (or maybe this is not benign at all?). Luckily after some time I felt less sensitive, but I guess now it is possible for me to kindle a healthy response to stress.

### Peertje80 — 2016-11-06T21:10:35+0200
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-203669>

I had a bit of an adjustment period to the shorter light days. Which resulted in a HS outbreak... but of course. My mood took a dive due to lack of adequate sun light. And day light savings time.... aarrrrrrrrg. But... now I'm actually doing quite well. Short summary of things:

-   New blueblocker glasses which are now plenty available in the Netherlands. These actually seem to work since I don't have carb cravings like I had last autumn.
-   We made some adjustments to lighting in the living.
-   Bathroom renovation is planned for January. In the blue print... LED lights are out (yeah).
-   Since the 1st of Novembre I'm back to work fulltime fully recouped from my mental and physical break down. I noticed however when slowly starting to return to work, that longer hours at the office drains energy quite clearly. I didn't really noticed this before as I do now.
-   I take longer breaks during work days, so I can take nice long walks outside. Yes even when it rains.
-   CT and grounding after returning home from work. 20 minutes with 1 foot in ice bucket, other foot grounding on the grass staring in the general direction of the sun.
-   Taking it easy, even choosing not to go kiting sometimes, canceling appointment and such to balance energy.
-   Sleeping 1 hour more, between 8 en 9 hours a night.
-   Meditating every day.
-   Because of autumn ... most carbs are out. Just some autumn fruit. And added in larger amount of fat. Still have a large appetite.
-   Writing in my journal everyday to get ride of negative shit.
-   Wrote my business plan and took step 1 to start my own creative business.
-   And still going strong studying to become a shiatsu therapist.
-   I now have days, sometimes weeks, without pain in my muscles and joints. This makes me feel so free. My muscle tension has improved so much
-   I have a normal stress response now... actually this is pretty inconvienent but I guess very healthy.

I feel I'm on the right track. It is not going as fast as I would like to. But this is my pace, slow and steady is okay. I'm bursting with energy. I don't recognize myself

Thanks you Dr. Kruse for you reprimand last year. I needed that. It got me of my ass, realizing I have to do this myself... every step of the way. Working hard to escape office slavery in nnEMF hell. At this pace this will be a reality for me in 2 years.

### Optimalbound — 2017-02-12T08:56:28+0200
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-208447>

Depends on distance etc., I suppose. I do not know enough about it to give sound advice, but 15 minutes a day sounds like a reasonable starting point for your biohack. It it increases your pain and discomfort rather than relieve it, it is probably wise to dial it down or end it altogether.

I think it has been mentioned that the risk of red light therapy causing fibrosis is higher if you do it in the evening, but I might be wrong on that.

### Peertje80 — 2018-08-26T10:52:32+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/guess-im-in.14134/post-249443>

Well I guess I was out... since my shoulder injury my life in relation to health became of track big time.

Since I couldn't go kitesurfing, I wasn't outside as much as I used to be. Drinking lotst of coffee, popping pain killers, not minding my water intake. Being inactive in general. Eating in front of tv… wtf. And I found a new job. The job is better for me stress wise, but working conditions are worse than in my old job. I have no natural lighting, no window with view outside. Sitting under bad lighting with 3 led screens in front of me. O jes, did I mention I work in a hospital now? Dr.K was right... not a good idea. Well at least I'm not sitting under a wifi router anymore. After 1 year of working there, I know I have to move on again.

Last winter I started to gain weight like crazy. My energy was like a roller costar... and I didn't even notice what was going on. In no time I was carb hooked and grazing all day. I had an eye infection in February(which I never have). This should have been the warning sign already. Before summer started I realized I became insulin resistant. I began to suffer from hearing strange sounds, dizzy spells, muscle stiffness and ocular migraines again. Starting August I was retaining fluid around my knees and fingers. The compression on the joints was unbearable. I could barely walk.

My MD ordered blood work and urine: nothing.... healthy as healthy can be. Even had vit D of 80. Which made me quite happy, though worried it is not high enough to get me through winter. She could not offer an explanation for my ordeal. But retaining fluid, she said, is not good. However no solution yet...

So I started Leptin rx in July again. Since then I already lost 5kg. I hope in time my other problems will magically disappear too. I feel I’m way too young to have these kind of problems. But I have seen with my own eyes now… disconnect from nature, enhance with some radiation is a sure ticket to hell.

I thought I could get a way with it for a while, but I cannot.

Or are there anything you can further optimize where you live, do you live in an own house or in an apartment? Do you have a nnEMF meter?

The Netherlands are really densely populated and have a lot of light pollution too, really bad when you watch on the map

Let us know how you do

# Thread: Is DNA the next internet... great article on biophoton repair et al -
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/is-dna-the-next-internet-great-article-on-biophoton-repair-et-al.14137/>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 3
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Penny — 2015-04-26T03:57:38+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/is-dna-the-next-internet-great-article-on-biophoton-repair-et-al.14137/post-162429>

[http://www.viewzone.com/dnax.html](http://www.viewzone.com/dnax.html)

Here is the start of the article:
"A Russian scientist, Pjotr Garjajev, had managed to intercept communication from a DNA molecule in the form of ultraviolet photons -- light! What's more, he claimed to have captured this communication from one organism (a frog embryo) with a laser beam and then transmitted it to another organisms DNA (a salamander embryo), causing the latter embryo to develop into a frog!

But this was just the beginning.

Dr. Garjajev claims that this communication is not something that happens only inside the individual cells or between one cell and another. He claims organisms use this "light" to "talk" to other organisms and suggested that this could explain telepathy and ESP. It was like human beings already had their own wireless internet based on our DNA. Wow!

{ "lightbox\_close": "Close", "lightbox\_next": "Next", "lightbox\_previous": "Previous", "lightbox\_error": "The requested content cannot be loaded. Please try again later.", "lightbox\_start\_slideshow": "Start slideshow", "lightbox\_stop\_slideshow": "Stop slideshow", "lightbox\_full\_screen": "Full screen", "lightbox\_thumbnails": "Thumbnails", "lightbox\_download": "Download", "lightbox\_share": "Share", "lightbox\_zoom": "Zoom", "lightbox\_new\_window": "New window", "lightbox\_toggle\_sidebar": "Toggle sidebar" }

I tried to find a scientific journal that had this experiment. All I could find were blogs and other websites that carried the same story, word for word, without any references. That is until I stumbled on the work of Fritz-Albert Popp \[**right**\]. Then everything I had just read seemed very plausible.

Fritz-Albert Popp thought he had discovered a cure for cancer. I'm not convinced that he didn't.

It was 1970, and Popp, a theoretical biophysicist at the University of Marburg in Germany, had been teaching radiology -- the interaction of electromagnetic (EM) radiation on biological systems. Popp was too early to worry about things like cellphones and microwave towers which are now commonly linked with cancers and leukemia. His world was much smaller.

He'd been examining two almost identical molecules: benzo\[a\]pyrene, a polycyclic hydrocarbon known to be one of the most lethal carcinogens to humans, and its twin (save for a tiny alteration in its molecular makeup), benzo\[e\]pyrene. He had illuminated both molecules with ultraviolet (UV) light in an attempt to find exactly what made these two almost identical molecules so different."

Anyway - it really made the light thing easier for me to fathom - it might help someone else here too

I am trying to figure out how artimisin and mistletoe help with the photorepair in the body - I googled:
"mistletoe biophoton repair" -

# Thread: Biophotons: the human body emits, communicates with, and is made from light
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/biophotons-the-human-body-emits-communicates-with-and-is-made-from-light.14138/>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 6
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Penny — 2015-04-26T04:13:37+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/biophotons-the-human-body-emits-communicates-with-and-is-made-from-light.14138/post-162430>

Interesting article - ties in to the last one I posted - loved this little snippet:

**"Meditation and Herbs Affect Biophoton Output**
Research has found an oxidative stress-mediated difference in biophoton emission among mediators versus non-meditators. Those who meditate regularly tend to have lower ultra-weak photon emission (UPE, biophoton emission), which is believed to result from the lower level of free radical reactions occurring in their bodies. In one clinical study involving practitioners of transcendental meditation (TM) researchers found:

The lowest UPE intensities were observed in two subjects who regularly meditate. Spectral analysis of human UPE has suggested that ultra-weak emission is probably, at least in part, a reflection of free radical reactions in a living system. It has been documented that various physiologic and biochemical shifts follow the long-term practice of meditation and it is inferred that meditation may impact free radical activity.\[13\]

Interestingly, an herb well-known for its use in stress reduction (including inducing measurable declines in cortisol), and associated heightened oxidative stress, has been tested clinically in reducing the level of biophotons emitted in human subjects. Known as [rhodiola](http://www.greenmedinfo.com/substance/rhodiola-tibetan-ginseng), a study published in 2009 in the journal _Phytotherapeutic Research_ found that those who took the herb for 1 week has a significant decrease in photon emission in comparison with the placebo group.\[14\]"

[http://drleonardcoldwell.com/2013/0...its-communicates-with-and-is-made-from-light/](http://drleonardcoldwell.com/2013/08/28/biophotons-the-human-body-emits-communicates-with-and-is-made-from-light/)

So, it seems to me if you are blue light toxic (MS), rhodiola might help you?

### Penny — 2015-04-26T06:21:00+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/biophotons-the-human-body-emits-communicates-with-and-is-made-from-light.14138/post-162439>

For what it's worth, rhodiola is grown in the Arctic... maybe it stores red light and that counteracts blue light? Weirdly, artimisn is grown in Africa -

# Thread: D.H.A. - Raw seafood vs. cooked

In one of Jack's latest podcasts he talks about how DHA is very susceptible to oxidation from light and heat. This made me realize the importance of eating seafood raw since it makes sense that the DHA would be retained.
I'm just wondering; If we cook our seafood, is any of the DHA retained at all?

If not, that means EVERYBODY is deficient in DHA! (unless you eat sushi)

Very good podcast, has some funny moments:

I am constantly in awe with just how much Jack knows! The "proof is in the pudding", so to speak.
You can tell that his OWN brain is working extremely sharp!

**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/d-h-a-raw-seafood-vs-cooked.14142/post-162510>

Take advantage of the fresh seafood here in Vancouver. There are several places downtown that have "buck a shuck" specials daily. Chewies and the Fish Shack downtown as well as Merchant oyster bar on commercial

### Jack Kruse — 2015-04-27T19:07:51+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-does-melatonin-and-leptin-couple.14155/post-162551>

Melatonin is filled with an aromatic ring. Your pictogram shows it in this blog. What does this mean? Only a few biomolecules that are good conductors. These tend to have aromatic rings, such as most of the hormones like melatonin, testosterone and progesterone. Recall that leptin action controls the release of all of these quantum critical biomolecules. Being quantum critical means the protein can control electrons in altered fields. Most of the molecules taking part actively in biochemical processes are tuned exactly to the transition point and are critical conductors for this very specific reason. The permutations of possible energy levels of biomolecules is huge so the possibility of finding even one that is in the quantum critical state by accident is mind-bogglingly small. The EM spectrum has 10 to the 73rd possible frequencies to control proteins but it turns out there are only 1,000,000 chemicals on Earth that have these electronic states with these abilities. These are the chemicals that the 3 kingdoms of life organize around. Once you focus your attention on their abilities you begin to see how the cosmic wand organized life at the most fundamental level. It is all about energy and energy states and charge. The electromagnetic spectrum is design to move charges of atoms or ions to give it a control feature. The innate fact that the electromagnetic force can exquisitely control electrons in proteins gives them the quantum critical features to innovate life from energy. The behavior of electrons in large molecules when they occupy the exotic state that sits at the knife’s edge between conduction and insulation is the critical piece, and it is the aromatic ring is one of the molecular footprints that point out why hormones all have it. Vitamin D3 and Vitamin A have it as well. And this explains why VDR and RXR work precisely with DHA. DHA can turn the suns light into an electric field to control the flow of these electrons. The electrons in biomolecule must be kept in in a state between freedom and control in the lattice. The atomic lattice configuration then sets the Rosetta stone control of incident light frequency that moves of holds the electrons to carry out physiologic abilities. When these molecules are conductors, some of their bound electrons are able to move freely under the influence of an electric field. By contrast, when these molecules are insulators, the electrons are not free to move and can withstand changes to environmental electric fields. The key to understand how they react to magnetic field alterations. These field alter electron spin…….and that does not require any movement. I have a deep sense this is where modern communication is affecting our quantum critical proteins in a deep unyielding fashion. We do not understand this connection in modern biology. We need to.

Excellent point about pregnenolone steal! For those who don't know, this is the diversion of the body's production of pregnenolone, a hormone precursor, to stress hormones like cortisol... which deprives the other hormones of this vital building block. And I understand our bodies also don't produce as much pregnenolone as we age. Another thing to be aware of.

# Thread: How to get the CT session cold enough?
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/>
**Subforum:** Cold Thermogenesis
**Posts:** 6
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### mark444200 — 2015-04-29T06:00:14+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162722>

Admittedly I don't know currently how cold my CT sessions are (I've got a skin thermometer on the way from ebay though). I've built up to 24 minutes in a pure-cold water bath with 6 or so ice packs chucked in it.

I imagine if the bath was filled with ice cubes it'd be much colder, but how do people get these ice cubes, do you have to buy them from an ice machine every day?

Interested in other peoples techniques / experiences. I guess another option would be an outdoor tub.. or to do it cheaply, like a drum of some description filled with water?

### Da-mo — 2015-04-29T06:12:02+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162723>

We bought a bunch of ice cube trays from a 2nd hand shop and just fill em and put them in the freezer.

I've found that the bought ice (the kind you buy in bags from gas stations etc.) tends not to cool the water as much - I'm sure they use water that is easier to freeze to use less power and as such it melts easier too.

We monitor the water temp using one of those floating swimming pool thermometers - cost $20 or so. Often take it to the waterfall as well so we can check the water temp there too.

Another thing to keep an eye on is skin color - that is a good indication too - see CT Protocol.

### Clayton — 2015-04-29T06:33:23+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162725>

Freeze 4 litre milk jugs and leave them in for a 1/2 hour before beggining your session

### fitness@home — 2015-04-29T12:36:57+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162762>

Since CT-ing in Texas can be a challenge for 8 months out of the year (hot here), I bought a chiller. In the past I have used frozen gallon jugs of water like Clayton. Fortunately we have a chest freezer and that made storage of them easier.

In our winter, I can use the pool outside. My husband just switched it over to a salt water system.

### nicld — 2015-04-29T16:19:08+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162767>

I do the milk jugs too in the summer. In winter I just have to set buckets outside for a bit and make sure they don't freeze solid.

### mark444200 — 2015-04-30T03:57:38+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/how-to-get-the-ct-session-cold-enough.14171/post-162808>

thanks for the info guys.

I also did some digging around myself and heres a video for those interested;

he adds salt to the water, then fills up water balloons to freeze and re-use. bigger surface area than the milk jugs? but a lot more work. he says putting salt in the water will make it colder.

# Thread: Fighting group think in the literature?

### Jack Kruse — 2015-04-29T20:04:35+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/fighting-group-think-in-the-literature.14193/post-162778>

[http://www.independent.co.uk/news/s...tered-says-former-editor-of-bmj-10196077.html](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/science/scientific-peer-reviews-are-a-sacred-cow-ready-to-be-slaughtered-says-former-editor-of-bmj-10196077.html)
